  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_87e8cd78-e3d4-43b3-bb75-e00660b12b2f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

Lost in his </span>
  <span id="freeText13726598168149056986" style="display:none">Three lives come together in unexpected and thrilling ways in Kate Atkinson's When Will There Be Good News?<br /><br />On a hot summer day, Joanna Mason's family slowly wanders home along a country lane. A moment later, Joanna's life is changed forever...<br /><br />On a dark night thirty years later, ex-detective Jackson Brodie finds himself on a train that is both crowded and late. Lost in his thoughts, he suddenly hears a shocking sound...<br /><br />At the end of a long day, 16-year-old Reggie is looking forward to watching a little TV. Then a terrifying noise shatters her peaceful evening. Luckily, Reggie makes it a point to be prepared for an emergency...<br /><br />These three lives come together in unexpected and deeply thrilling ways in the latest novel from Kate Atkinson, the critically acclaimed author who Harlan Coben calls "an absolute must-read."</span>

      </div>

<div id="review_1982103207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1982103207" />
    <a title="Jaline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7234171-jaline"><img alt="Jaline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530498058p2/7234171.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1982103207?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaline" href="/user/show/7234171-jaline">Jaline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7234171-jaline?shelf=2019-completed">2019-completed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1982103207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4221151674723852771">Once again, Kate Atkinson has written a novel that fires off with sketched pencil outlines that gradually become filled in, fleshed out with colours both brilliant and ominous.<br/><br/>In this third (of five, so far) Jackson Brodie novel, we become re-acquainted with several returning characters. As I observed in her last novel, these characters are like streamers floating in an uncertain breeze suspended from a common source – a maypole perhaps – each one with their own backstory, their own tragic or sa</span>
  <span id="freeText4221151674723852771" style="display:none">Once again, Kate Atkinson has written a novel that fires off with sketched pencil outlines that gradually become filled in, fleshed out with colours both brilliant and ominous.<br /><br />In this third (of five, so far) Jackson Brodie novel, we become re-acquainted with several returning characters. As I observed in her last novel, these characters are like streamers floating in an uncertain breeze suspended from a common source – a maypole perhaps – each one with their own backstory, their own tragic or sad or serendipitous histories. As the breeze becomes a wind, the streamers touch each other – briefly – or sometimes become stuck together for a time until the wind changes direction and they touch others, clinging or bouncing off in another direction.<br /><br />The intricacy of this dance among her characters is what sets Kate Atkinson’s writing apart. The connections are rarely obvious, and sometimes they are hazy and unclear, yet as I sat riveted by this story I remained hypnotized by the ballet being played out in front of my eyes.<br /><br />This novel is set largely in Scotland, in and around Edinburgh with some Glaswegian thugs thrown in for good measure. <br /><br />There is a new character, too – a young girl named Regina (“call me Reggie”) who is 16 years old, looks like she’s 11 or 12, and has the mind, capacity for love, and loyalties of a person twice her age. Reggie is the pivot point for this novel as she is linked, either directly or indirectly, to the majority of the other characters in the story.<br /><br />It is Reggie who is the true heroine of this novel as she invests every ounce of her being into saving lives, finding lost things (and people), and guarding those she loves and cares about with ferocious intelligence.<br /><br />Jackson Brodie’s own life takes many subtle, sudden, and surprising twists. He loses almost everything in his life and paradoxically, he regains not just himself, but a closer sense of who he really is; of all that matters most to him.<br /><br />Once again, I am eager to return to the world inhabited by Jackson Brodie and his many acquaintances and his few close friends. I plan to read the 4th novel in this series early in June, and while the 5th in the series will be published late in June, I hope to read that one as soon as I can after it is published.<br /><br />This is gripping, suspenseful writing with fascinating characters whose lives and philosophies may differ from each other, yet each one authentically painted in their own colours, and so real I feel I know them personally. It doesn’t get much better than this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4221151674723852771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2818187218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2818187218" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2818187218?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2818187218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2009314697551119989">It's a joy to return to Kate Atkinson's rather unusual offbeat crime series featuring Jackson Brodie, full of wry wit and humour, and her trademark case studies of the lives of the main characters. It is a story in which for the characters, the title of the novel is particularly apt, given the horror, trauma and tragedies that have blighted their lives. In a rural part of Devon, 6 year old Joanna is to have her life ripped apart by horrors that no-one should ever have to experience, which result</span>
  <span id="freeText2009314697551119989" style="display:none">It's a joy to return to Kate Atkinson's rather unusual offbeat crime series featuring Jackson Brodie, full of wry wit and humour, and her trademark case studies of the lives of the main characters. It is a story in which for the characters, the title of the novel is particularly apt, given the horror, trauma and tragedies that have blighted their lives. In a rural part of Devon, 6 year old Joanna is to have her life ripped apart by horrors that no-one should ever have to experience, which result in her being the only family member to survive. Thirty years later, the person convicted of the nightmare crimes is being released from prison. 16 year old Regina 'Reggie' Chase is nanny to a GP's baby, the mother has gone missing with her baby, and Reggie seems to be the only one who is worried about this. Reggie's tenacity and determination bring in the recently married Chief Inspector Louise Monroe, and the ex-cop and PI Jackson Brodie with his family problems, with the two mired in their own tangled relationship. In a story that celebrates the everyday routines and actions, and great cultural references, it is the remarkable presence of hope, and the spirit of human resilience in the face of the horrors and traumatic challenges that life can throw at a person. that shines through. A wonderful addition to simply brilliant series. Many thanks to Random House Transworld for a copy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2009314697551119989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2817011708" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2817011708" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63168028-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516912354p2/63168028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2817011708?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/63168028-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2817011708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14930421614328044661"><b>Circumstance</b><br/><i>When Will There Be Good News?</i> is a thriller from the wonderful Kate Atkinson that is the third book in the Jackson Brodie series but can be read as a standalone. The novel is full of suspense, surprises and a fair splattering of coincidence. The opening scene shocked me! Kate Atkinson writes with an unrestrained scope and mixes a fascinating plot with great characters. She teases us with humour while masking the opportunity of dropping cruel murderous bombshells. The plot is a mix of</span>
  <span id="freeText14930421614328044661" style="display:none"><b>Circumstance</b><br /><i>When Will There Be Good News?</i> is a thriller from the wonderful Kate Atkinson that is the third book in the Jackson Brodie series but can be read as a standalone. The novel is full of suspense, surprises and a fair splattering of coincidence. The opening scene shocked me! Kate Atkinson writes with an unrestrained scope and mixes a fascinating plot with great characters. She teases us with humour while masking the opportunity of dropping cruel murderous bombshells. The plot is a mix of multiple threads that start weaving in and out of each other and what I liked is that it happens throughout the novel rather than all coming at once. The plot is cloaked in misdirection and tentative assumptions.<br /><br />Thirty years after serving a prison sentence for the murder of the Mason family, where only 6-year-old Joanne was left alive, Andrew Decker, the killer, has gone underground and Dr Joanne Hunter (nee Mason) has gone missing with her infant baby. Reggie Chase, Dr Hunter’s baby-minder and friend, finds herself in the middle of a complex web of events. Thrown into the web of murder and deceit, along with the gutsy Reggie, are Chief Inspector Louise Monroe and ex-soldier, ex-cop, current PI, Jackson Brodie. Each character is developed with great depth and capacity, but I loved the character of Reggie, she is 16 years of age, feisty, resilient and clever. A young girl that hasn’t had much luck in life, in fact, when has there ever been good news. <blockquote>
  <i> “Just because something bad happened to her once doesn’t mean it’s happened again,’ Louise said to Reggie. ‘No,’ Reggie said. ‘You’re wrong. Just because something bad happened to her once doesn’t mean it won’t happen again. Believe me, bad things happen to me all the time.’ ‘Me too,’ Jackson said.”</i>
</blockquote> An implicit reference to the title.<br /><br />The personal relationships with spouses, friends and colleagues, felt very real, with wonderful subtleties that were just masterstrokes. The love interest was engaging and tantalising – why is it that we often want what we shouldn’t have. Marriages, in particular, are put under tremendous strain throughout the book and often the thing most valued, isn’t the person sharing the home.<br /><br />Kate Atkinson provides amazing detail and observations, often with a bit of humour. <blockquote>
  <i> “A few supermarket lorries thundered along and a speeding motorcyclist hurtled past, eager to donate an organ in time for someone’s Christmas.”</i>
</blockquote> If I had one criticism it would be that sometimes the detail feels like she has veered off-track and delivered content that didn’t really mean much.<br /><br />I would highly recommend this book and I’d like to thank Random House UK, Transworld Publishers and NetGalley for providing me with an ARC copy in return for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14930421614328044661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_48997136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48997136" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48997136?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48997136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12611249864690779708">so, when i heard kate atkinson had a new book i thought "yayyy!!" and then when i found out it was another jackson brodie novel i said "boooo!!" i thought the first one was great, but the second was a lot weaker. there's a reason i tend not to read genre fiction like sci-fi and mystery - because i just don't want to commit to ten books about the same world. i would rather read one book that is self-contained and never visit the characters again.(and yes i know - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/159630.Donald_Harington' title='Donald Harington' rel='nofollow noopener'>Donald Harington</a> is exempt from t</span>
  <span id="freeText12611249864690779708" style="display:none">so, when i heard kate atkinson had a new book i thought "yayyy!!" and then when i found out it was another jackson brodie novel i said "boooo!!" i thought the first one was great, but the second was a lot weaker. there's a reason i tend not to read genre fiction like sci-fi and mystery - because i just don't want to commit to ten books about the same world. i would rather read one book that is self-contained and never visit the characters again.(and yes i know - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/159630.Donald_Harington" title="Donald Harington" rel="nofollow noopener">Donald Harington</a> is exempt from this preference because no one can write like him) that being said - i loved this book. it's true that there seem to be a lot of characters in atkinson's books who have all had one or more family members murdered in horrible ways, which seems like an unlikely coincidence, path-crossing-wise, but she really can do it all - write a convincing multi-plot mystery novel with exceptionally interesting and flawed characters, as well as a pretty incisive psychological study of these people. so - jackson brodie redeemed, which is good i suppose, since it doesn't seem like this will be the end of this character. i'm in it for the long haul now.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

<div id="review_790722146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/790722146" />
    <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma"><img alt="PattyMacDotComma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577835191p2/1128612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/790722146?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PattyMacDotComma" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma">PattyMacDotComma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=mystery-crime-thriller">mystery-crime-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=favourites-adult">favourites-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=aa">aa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=arc-netgalley-done">arc-netgalley-done</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer790722146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17822815809591039805"><b>5★<br/>“Twenty years ago she too would have found his moodiness attractive. Now she just wanted to punch him. But then she seemed to want to punch everyone at the moment.”</b><br/><br/>There’s a lot to be angry about in this third of Atkinson’s Jackson Brodie series, and there were plenty of times I wanted to punch somebody too – or worse. In this instance, she is Detective Chief Inspector Louse Monroe, and he is a man suspected of fraud who’s just opened his front door and smiled sarcastically at her warrant card</span>
  <span id="freeText17822815809591039805" style="display:none"><b>5★<br />“Twenty years ago she too would have found his moodiness attractive. Now she just wanted to punch him. But then she seemed to want to punch everyone at the moment.”</b><br /><br />There’s a lot to be angry about in this third of Atkinson’s Jackson Brodie series, and there were plenty of times I wanted to punch somebody too – or worse. In this instance, she is Detective Chief Inspector Louse Monroe, and he is a man suspected of fraud who’s just opened his front door and smiled sarcastically at her warrant card. I remember Louise from a past story, and there’s no way I would be looking sideways at her warrant card! <br /><br />Hers is one thread of a story with many remarkably inventive intersections. Jackson is the main character, of course, and finds himself in Edinburgh despite his intention to have a nice, peaceful life with his lovely new wife. No stress. <br /><br />But fortunately for us, Atkinson’s not going to let him off that easily. He’s a sucker for a damsel in distress, and it seems most of them are.<br /><br /><b>“<i>‘You used to be a private detective. Right?’</i> she said.<br /> <br /><i>‘Amongst other things.’</i> <br /><br />‘So you used to find people?’ <br /><br />‘Sometimes. I also lost people.’ &lt;”</b><br /><br />She’s not buying that. She is Reggie, a 16-year old schoolgirl, orphaned now with only her self-styled gangster brother, Billy, who's been beating up on her since childhood. But lately she has been very happy as mother’s help for well-to-do Dr Hunter and her baby boy, the three of them forming a tight, happy little unit. <br /><br /><b>“<i>‘How’s my treasure?</i>’ Dr Hunter asked, nuzzling the baby’s neck (<i>‘He’s edible, don’t you think?’</i>) and Reggie felt something seize in her heart, a little convulsion of pain, and she wasn’t sure why exactly except that she thought it was sad (very sad indeed) that no one could remember being a baby. What Reggie wouldn’t have given to have been a baby, wrapped in Mum’s arms again. Or Dr Hunter’s arms, for that matter. Anyone’s arms really. Not Billy’s obviously.”</b><br /><br />And the pay is pretty good, so things are looking up. Until this.<br /><br /><b>“She’d identified a dead body, had her flat vandalized, been threatened by violent idiots and it wasn’t even lunchtime. Reggie hoped the rest of the day would be more uneventful.”</b><br /><br />Of course, Atkinson’s back stories are always intriguing to the point that once I get caught up in one, it’s a shock to find myself back in the present and then, next thing I know, I’m deep into someone else’s history. Wonderful stuff! <br /><br />Her style is her own, and I love it – the surprising juxtaposition of ideas, the everyday and the exceptional, all thrown in together. <br /><br /><b>“Everything about her life was just lovely. Apart from the whole family massacred in childhood thing.”</b><br /><br />I don’t know how she combines affection with disdain, but while I’m snickering knowingly behind my hand at some dowdy character, I’m also kind of warming to them.<br /><br /><b>“The therapist, a hippyish, well-intentioned woman called Jenny who looked as if she’d knitted herself. . . ”</b><br /><br />She’s quite a contrast to Ms MacDonald, an unwell lady who’s helping Reggie with her school studies. <br /><br /><b>“Ms MacDonald was in her fifties but she had never been young. When she was a teacher at the school she looked as if she ironed herself every morning.”</b><br /><br />And then there’s a woman on the train <b>“leafing indifferently through a celebrity magazine, was a fortyish blonde, buxom as an overstuffed turkey. She was wearing siren-red lipstick and a top to match that was half a size too tight and which burned like a signal fire in front of Jackson’s eyes. Jackson was surprised she didn’t have <i>‘Up for It</i>’ tattooed on her forehead.”</b><br /><br />Jackson’s love for his daughter Marlee and his affection for wives and women in his past all mingle together. Also mingled together are his memories of the army, the police force, and his private cases. Under it all is his sorrow.<br /><br /><b>“Not his real home, his real home, the one he never named any more, was the dark and sooty chamber in his heart that contained his sister and his brother and, because it was an accommodating kind of space, the entire filthy history of the industrial revolution. It was amazing how much dark matter you could crush inside the black hole of the heart.”</b><br /><br />This current story touches on all of them and then some. I love it, but then I’m a pushover for everything she writes, I think. This was a re-read before I read the latest, #5, so thanks to NetGalley and Random House/Transworld/Black Swan for the copy for review. Even if I’d remembered critical plot points (which I admit I hadn’t), I’d have enjoyed it just as much for her writing alone.<br /><br />P.S. I should add that I think you can enjoy this on its own without having read the previous books. Atkinson answers any questions you might have. Of course, I like to read them in order, but if this is the only one you can get your hands on - do so!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17822815809591039805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9471409714632200684">This book is grim, violent, sad (dead kids, dead moms, dead dogs), and also hilarious and uplifting (passionate cops, a ferociously maternal doctor, and a heroic dog who makes it all the way through -- sorry if that's a spoiler, but I would have wanted to know.) The character of 16-year-old Reggie should be given a special literary prize for Best Plucky Orphan Since Oliver Twist. Deeply satisfying and I can't wait for the next one.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3798699574644090784">I am steadily rereading my way through the Jackson Brodie novels to prepare myself for the latest release, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43107933.Big_Sky__Jackson_Brodie___5_' title='Big Sky (Jackson Brodie, #5) by Kate Atkinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Big Sky</a>. And it is so much fun! Don't forget that I am one of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10015.Kate_Atkinson' title='Kate Atkinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kate Atkinson</a>'s biggest fans so if I rave a bit, forgive me. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3289281.When_Will_There_Be_Good_News___Jackson_Brodie___3_' title='When Will There Be Good News? (Jackson Brodie, #3) by Kate Atkinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>When Will There Be Good News?</a>is Kate at her very best. The story is intriguing, beginning with a mass murder with one survivor, a small six year old girl called Joanna. Fast forward to thirty years later and Joanna is the well respected Dr.Hunter, living in an expensive</span>
  <span id="freeText3798699574644090784" style="display:none">I am steadily rereading my way through the Jackson Brodie novels to prepare myself for the latest release, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43107933.Big_Sky__Jackson_Brodie___5_" title="Big Sky (Jackson Brodie, #5) by Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Big Sky</a>. And it is so much fun! Don't forget that I am one of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10015.Kate_Atkinson" title="Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Atkinson</a>'s biggest fans so if I rave a bit, forgive me. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3289281.When_Will_There_Be_Good_News___Jackson_Brodie___3_" title="When Will There Be Good News? (Jackson Brodie, #3) by Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener">When Will There Be Good News?</a>is Kate at her very best. The story is intriguing, beginning with a mass murder with one survivor, a small six year old girl called Joanna. Fast forward to thirty years later and Joanna is the well respected Dr.Hunter, living in an expensive house in a good area with a (rather dodgy) husband, a baby and a dog. <br /><br />In typical fashion the author then introduces more lovely new characters, including the fabulous Reggie, and a couple more story lines, as well as bringing in Jackson Brodie and his love interest from the previous book, Chief Inspector Louise Monroe. You need to concentrate as there is layer upon layer upon layer and coincidences abound. Eventually we discover that some of the characters have hidden depths, several people suffer very unpleasant deaths and a lot of what happens is never discovered by the police! It is all wrapped up very nicely at the end.<br /><br />It is all so much more than a simple murder mystery. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10015.Kate_Atkinson" title="Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Atkinson</a> gives us interesting and well rounded characters who we care about. She takes us on a journey which at first seems to be going in all directions but then little by little she draws everything together to an excellent conclusion, and if you are anything like me at all you sit back and say "Now that was a GOOD book!"<br /></span>

<div id="review_37583451" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37583451" />
    <a title="Dagný" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/418131-dagn"><img alt="Dagný" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309701851p2/418131.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37583451?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dagný" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dagný" href="/user/show/418131-dagn">Dagný</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37583451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15531733480406178422">Here is a book which one reads paradoxically wishing it never ended- because it is so good- yet one races to finish- being compelled to- without skipping a word.<br/><br/>My heart was aching for the main characters to come through and survive; for the good to prevail; for some things to go right. This was so suspenseful, more so than anything I have read lately.<br/><br/>Never thought Loeb's green classics, which I can see sitting pretty on a shelf, would be referenced in a suspense novel. It is a part of the pleas</span>
  <span id="freeText15531733480406178422" style="display:none">Here is a book which one reads paradoxically wishing it never ended- because it is so good- yet one races to finish- being compelled to- without skipping a word.<br /><br />My heart was aching for the main characters to come through and survive; for the good to prevail; for some things to go right. This was so suspenseful, more so than anything I have read lately.<br /><br />Never thought Loeb's green classics, which I can see sitting pretty on a shelf, would be referenced in a suspense novel. It is a part of the pleasure of reading this book that the hard-scrabble main characters are smart and well read; their thoughts have a cultural reference and they are not stick figures. Rather they are mordantly witty, interesting and good people, in spite of the burdens they carry.<br /><br />Implicitly the author, Kate Atkinson is always thinking, asking hard questions, and giving unconventional answers. Very good company indeed.<br /><br />The plot is intricate and cleverly spun and its great fun to see how the strands are woven together. <br /><br />This is an excellent book.<br /><br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15531733480406178422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_39837646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39837646" />
    <a title="Rorie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/773235-rorie"><img alt="Rorie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39837646?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rorie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rorie" href="/user/show/773235-rorie">Rorie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39837646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12607971650689368933">The whole time I was reading this book, I kept waiting for something to actually happen and make sense.   <span id="freeText12607971650689368933" style="display:none">The whole time I was reading this book, I kept waiting for something to actually happen and make sense. The only reason why I kept reading the book is because I didn't have anything else to read at the time, and I kept thinking that it had to get better.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/216284-mark?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30799499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7189815100588257752"><br/>Kate Atkinson returns to form in the third book in her Jackson Brodie series. With her usual mix of strong mystery plot elements and finely drawn relationships, "When Will There Be Good News" fairly hums along, and it works even better in this case because Jackson Brodie, the former cop turned private eye turned rich pensioner, is not actually the centerpiece of this novel.<br/><br/>If there is a hero and fulcrum of this book, it is the wonderful new character of Reggie Chase, a 16-year-old who looks as t</span>
  <span id="freeText7189815100588257752" style="display:none"><br />Kate Atkinson returns to form in the third book in her Jackson Brodie series. With her usual mix of strong mystery plot elements and finely drawn relationships, "When Will There Be Good News" fairly hums along, and it works even better in this case because Jackson Brodie, the former cop turned private eye turned rich pensioner, is not actually the centerpiece of this novel.<br /><br />If there is a hero and fulcrum of this book, it is the wonderful new character of Reggie Chase, a 16-year-old who looks as though she's 13 and sounds as though she's 40. In fact, the only reason I didn't give this five stars is that Reggie almost seems too precocious at times, which didn't make me enjoy her any the less.<br /><br />Reggie has lost her mother in an accident, her brother is a juvenile delinquent fast becoming a hardened criminal, and she is now fending for herself, spending much of her time with her new mother figure, Dr. Joanna Hunter, who has hired Reggie as a mother's helper for her new baby.<br /><br />Dr. Hunter has a deep secret of her own, one that Reggie doesn't learn until near the end of the book, but one that shapes the young doctor's actions in ways that will forever alter the lives of all the book's characters.<br /><br />Throw into the mix one of Jackson Brodie's past flames, detective Louise Monroe, and Jackson's new wife, about whom he really knows very little, and the doctor's husband's problems with the underworld, and a bizarre train crash, and you have a snorter of a novel: Fast paced, well told, and lifted into a delightful place by young Reggie.<br /><br />As Reggie herself might say, if you asked her whether this was worth reading: "Och, yes: Sweartogod."</span>
  <a data-text-id="7189815100588257752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>,

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4010186578119559958">This book made me laugh and cry more than once, so it gets my vote. I felt the vividness of Atkinson's talent with the first in the series, Case Histories, but that one felt a bit contrived and manipulative to me. This one, the third, maybe does both, but it was a much more fun ride because of the emotional engagement it achieved for me. It plucks the heart strings with its 16 year-old heroine Reggie, whose love for the missing Dr. Hunter and the baby she serves as nanny moves her to many brave </span>
  <span id="freeText4010186578119559958" style="display:none">This book made me laugh and cry more than once, so it gets my vote. I felt the vividness of Atkinson's talent with the first in the series, Case Histories, but that one felt a bit contrived and manipulative to me. This one, the third, maybe does both, but it was a much more fun ride because of the emotional engagement it achieved for me. It plucks the heart strings with its 16 year-old heroine Reggie, whose love for the missing Dr. Hunter and the baby she serves as nanny moves her to many brave actions. The some-time detective Jackson Brodie and the Scottish Chief Inspector Louise Monroe are dragged into the case through Reggie's persistence, and their unrequited affection for each other makes a warm underground river of life against the cold forces of death. Atkinson is a master at rendering the stream of consciousness and emotional spheres of four characters who all orbit around the case and eventually converge. I was very engaged by the liveliness of these minds embedded in mundane activities and frequent tapping cultural reservoirs such as songs and literature. All have experienced past tragedies in the form violent deaths in their family in childhood Though persistently light and ironic in tone, the tale makes a realistic case for good people (and a good dog) making something real and strong in this perilous life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4010186578119559958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1336797335" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1336797335" />
    <a title="Paul E. Morph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44824883-paul-e-morph"><img alt="Paul E. Morph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602970987p2/44824883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1336797335?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul E. Morph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul E. Morph" href="/user/show/44824883-paul-e-morph">Paul E. Morph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/5429567-when-will-there-be-good-news">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44824883-paul-e-morph?shelf=books-read-in-2016">books-read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1336797335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14775310251632418161">My enjoyment of Kate Atkinson's Jackson Brodie novels increases with each book. You only have to look at my ratings: I gave the first one three stars, the second one four stars and now I find I can't not give this third volume five out of five.<br/><br/>This book begins with a horrific multiple murder and things go downhill from there. I kid, I kid... After the grisly opening, we jump forward thirty years to present day to see what the sole survivor of the initiating incident's life looks like now. While </span>
  <span id="freeText14775310251632418161" style="display:none">My enjoyment of Kate Atkinson's Jackson Brodie novels increases with each book. You only have to look at my ratings: I gave the first one three stars, the second one four stars and now I find I can't not give this third volume five out of five.<br /><br />This book begins with a horrific multiple murder and things go downhill from there. I kid, I kid... After the grisly opening, we jump forward thirty years to present day to see what the sole survivor of the initiating incident's life looks like now. While she has outwardly got her life together (far more than I have in fact) the news that the murderer she escaped three decades ago is being released from prison, having served his 'life' sentence, is sure to put the cat among even the most robust pigeons.<br /><br />Atkinson's writing has got such a wonderful rhythm to it (it verges on poetry in places) that it's almost hypnotic. One must resist the temptation to drift off, though, as this book is definitely one which rewards careful reading. All the plot threads are resolved by the end of the book, some for the better, some not so much, but if you're not paying attention you might not realise it.<br /><br />One of the themes of the book is the nature of our existence and what role coincidence and/or fate plays. Atkinson clearly delights in playing with the inter-connectedness of all things and obviously wants the reader to ponder how these things differ in fiction and 'real life'.<br /><br />The characters in this novel live and breathe and squirm their way into your head. I really cared what happened to these people over the course of the story and there are a couple of new characters in this book that I'm really hoping will turn up in the next one. I found myself genuinely scared for them in places and mourned with them in others. I also laughed with them at times because, while these books aren't comedies (except perhaps in the Shakespearian sense), nobody could deny that the author has a wry sense of humour that permeates her work.<br /><br />All in all, I'm now overjoyed I persevered with this series, which is not often the case when the first book is only a three star read. I'm very much looking forward to reading the fourth book in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14775310251632418161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2759212980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer534532256666805895">It's hard to categorize a Kate Atkinson detective/mystery novel- they really are so much more. To me they are literary novels with some mysteries within their pages. Why I love this series- They are intricately plotted with interesting characters and storylines.<br/>This is the third in the Jackson Brodie novels. I think it has been the best so far and I loved all three. He is definitely not the only person we encounter in this book. We meet Detective Chief Inspector Louise Monroe. She and Jackson us</span>
  <span id="freeText534532256666805895" style="display:none">It's hard to categorize a Kate Atkinson detective/mystery novel- they really are so much more. To me they are literary novels with some mysteries within their pages. Why I love this series- They are intricately plotted with interesting characters and storylines.<br />This is the third in the Jackson Brodie novels. I think it has been the best so far and I loved all three. He is definitely not the only person we encounter in this book. We meet Detective Chief Inspector Louise Monroe. She and Jackson used to work together before he left the police force. She is a driven and determined police officer, who worries about her cases and lives for her job. We also meet Reggie, a 16 yr old who is worried about her boss, Dr. Hunter, and does some sleuthing of her own. The author brings all these characters to life. She is such a clever writer!<br />I hated finishing this book as I wanted it to go on, but at the same time, I could not stop reading!!<br />I would highly recommend this book, but I would read them in sequence. It's better to get to know Jackson from book 1- Case Histories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="534532256666805895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trin" href="/user/show/113980-trin">Trin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33846526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9339792412890701591">Oh, stab me in the heart some more, Kate. Atkinson’s Jackson Brodie novels (the trilogy that begins with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16243.Case_Histories__Jackson_Brodie__1_' title='Case Histories (Jackson Brodie #1) by Kate Atkinson' rel='nofollow noopener'> Case Histories</a>) just get more and more depressing. This latest is simply <i>brutal</i>. And yet…I loved reading it, in spite of how bleak it is, in spite of the fact that the plot relies on some rather ridiculous Dickensian coincidences, in spite of Atkinson’s apparent hatred of semi-colons and love of comma splices. I’m not sure what it is, exactly, but I just love the way Atkinson’s characters le</span>
  <span id="freeText9339792412890701591" style="display:none">Oh, stab me in the heart some more, Kate. Atkinson’s Jackson Brodie novels (the trilogy that begins with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16243.Case_Histories__Jackson_Brodie__1_" title="Case Histories (Jackson Brodie #1) by Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener"> Case Histories</a>) just get more and more depressing. This latest is simply <i>brutal</i>. And yet…I loved reading it, in spite of how bleak it is, in spite of the fact that the plot relies on some rather ridiculous Dickensian coincidences, in spite of Atkinson’s apparent hatred of semi-colons and love of comma splices. I’m not sure what it is, exactly, but I just love the way Atkinson’s characters leap off the page, the way their voices crackle and spark and echo in my head. I love the way she writes. She remains one of those authors who can in effect do no wrong: I will read anything she puts to paper. (Got old grocery lists? Send ’em to me!) But, uh…try to write something a <i>little</i> lighter next time, Kate, okay? For my sake?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9339792412890701591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12377955887022220736">This is a decidedly 4.5 stars (come on Goodreads, sometimes a girl needs a half!). The two words that come to mind with this book are "clever" and "unexpected". The characters in the book were incredibly different and flawed in such differing ways, but the tying together of them reminded me (well, loosely) of the movie Love Actually. I loved some (Dr. Hunter, Reggie) and vascilated loving and hating some (Jackson & Louise), and of course, straight up hated the some others. But the attention to t</span>
  <span id="freeText12377955887022220736" style="display:none">This is a decidedly 4.5 stars (come on Goodreads, sometimes a girl needs a half!). The two words that come to mind with this book are "clever" and "unexpected". The characters in the book were incredibly different and flawed in such differing ways, but the tying together of them reminded me (well, loosely) of the movie Love Actually. I loved some (Dr. Hunter, Reggie) and vascilated loving and hating some (Jackson &amp; Louise), and of course, straight up hated the some others. But the attention to the plot and characterization drew me in. There were many moments of casual reading where I thought, "Wait. WHAT?" and went back to re-read what I read because I was shocked. Very different from many books I've read, and thus, very enjoyable.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/255113858?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/4542979-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11398272-when-will-there-be-good-news">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=buddy-reads-with-jemidar">buddy-reads-with-jemidar</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer255113858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9854337462839209709"><br/>I often have problems with crime fiction series. I love the idea of returning to an interesting world in the company of a well-loved character, but often the expectation of enjoyment engendered by the previous books in a series doesn't continue to be met. Well, with this series it's a matter of so far, so good. In fact, maybe it's so far, so much better. Admittedly, this is only Atkinson's third novel to feature Jackson Brodie, but it is probably my favourite to date. <br/><br/>This is not traditional cri</span>
  <span id="freeText9854337462839209709" style="display:none"><br />I often have problems with crime fiction series. I love the idea of returning to an interesting world in the company of a well-loved character, but often the expectation of enjoyment engendered by the previous books in a series doesn't continue to be met. Well, with this series it's a matter of so far, so good. In fact, maybe it's so far, so much better. Admittedly, this is only Atkinson's third novel to feature Jackson Brodie, but it is probably my favourite to date. <br /><br />This is not traditional crime fiction. The action does not always focus on Jackson Brodie and he doesn't necessarily resolve all of the issues. In this novel, he shares the action with Reggie (a smart, resourceful teenager) and Joanna (the survivor of horrific childhood events). As with the earlier novels in the series, Atkinson moves the narrative along using shifting perspectives and overlapping time frames. The plot relies heavily on random connections and the layering of coincidences. In the hands of a less skilled writer, this could lead to some heavy eye-rolling. However, in my view, Atkinson makes it work. The sense of life being a puzzle, where the different pieces appear unconnected but are all required to complete the picture is a theme of Atkinson's writing; it's kind of like a literary six degrees of separation game. The fact the Atkinson writes clear, elegant prose and realistic (and often very witty) dialogue also contributes to the quality of the work.<br /><br />Atkinson's style will not appeal to everyone. A reader whose taste runs to traditional police procedural style crime fiction may not like her books at all. A reader who struggles with random coincidences being an essential part of the narrative may dismiss the plot as completely implausible - which it is, on any close (or even not so close) analysis. But Atkinson's style appeals to me a lot. I like that even her most appealing characters are flawed. I like that she does not tie up everything in a neat bundle, but leaves some things unexplained. That can be unsettling in crime fiction, but it's the way it is in life. <br /><br />It's going to take me a while to tire of this series. In fact, there's every chance I won't tire of Jackson Brodie and his world for as long as Atkinson chooses to keep creating it. I'm looking forward to reading the next book in the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7307795.Started_Early__Took_My_Dog" title="Started Early, Took My Dog by Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Started Early, Took My Dog</a>.<br /><br />This was a most enjoyable buddy read with my friends Jemidar and Anna. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9854337462839209709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_35258853" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35258853" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1177534-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593697601p2/1177534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35258853?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1177534-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35258853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13596225317931492975">While walking home one day, six-year-old Joanna Mason's family is attacked and killed by a man wielding a butcher knife. Joanna escapes by fleeing into a cornfield and hiding. She's eventually found and the killer is caught and sent to jail.<br/><br/>Now before you get upset with me for revealing too much, let me just say that all of what I described above happens in the first twenty or so pages of Kate Atkinson's latest novel "When Will There Be Good News?" The death of Joanna's family is the catalyst fo</span>
  <span id="freeText13596225317931492975" style="display:none">While walking home one day, six-year-old Joanna Mason's family is attacked and killed by a man wielding a butcher knife. Joanna escapes by fleeing into a cornfield and hiding. She's eventually found and the killer is caught and sent to jail.<br /><br />Now before you get upset with me for revealing too much, let me just say that all of what I described above happens in the first twenty or so pages of Kate Atkinson's latest novel "When Will There Be Good News?" The death of Joanna's family is the catalyst for everything that happens for the rest of the story and the impact is felt on every single character we meet over the course of this story.<br /><br />As usual, Atkinson's novel is one that defies easy description. It's one part a mystery, one part character study and one part suspense thriller. The story starts out on a deceptively slow note, allowing readers to get to know the various players in the events to come and slowly building to a train wreck (literally and figuratively) of a turning point that has a direct impact on each of the characters. Atkinson brings back Jackson Brodie, the private detective who featured in her previous novels "Case Histories" and "One Good Turn" as well as several other familiar faces. <br /><br />As I read this story, comparions to Elizabeth George kept creeping up on me. (And that's a good thing as George is one of my favorite authors). Atkinson has a storytelling style that highlights characters, but continues to build the story with each page. She's subtle, working in details to the storyline naturally and rewarding readers when a payoff comes several pages later. Watching the story unfold, building up momentum until we finally see the bigger picture is fascinating. Several storylines cross over and we get to see events from several points of view.<br /><br />The various elements will keep you guessing, keep you curious and keep the pages turning. I consumed this book eagerly, anxious to find out what happens next. It's one of those where once the final page is turned, you'll walk away satisfied but wishing there was more to savor. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13596225317931492975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9930050184641820824" style="display:none">Jackson Brodie #3<br /><br />Six year old Joanna Mason was the only person to escape when a madman killed her mother, sister and baby brother. Now, thirty years later,Joanna is a successful Doctor with a baby of her own. The madman is being released from prison after serving his sentence. Jackson Brodie is an ex-policeman who is now retired but still does some investigative work. Louise is a stickler to the rules policewoman. There are three separate storylines in this book and in parts I found it confusing. There is also quite a few characters. The story starts off quite slow but picks up its pace just under half way through. I felt this was more about dysfunctional families rather than a detective story. I did like some of the characters who were true to life. There are a few twists to look out for. This is a decent enough read.<br /><br />I would like to thank NetGalley, Random House UK, Transworld Publishers and the author Kate Atkinson for my ARC in exchange for an honest review.</span>

<div id="review_95406924" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95406924" />
    <a title="James Thane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane"><img alt="James Thane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442513566p2/3483907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95406924?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Thane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Thane" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane">James Thane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95406924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14400351877946674320">Joanna Mason, a six-year-old girl, was the only person to escape when a madman killed her mother, sister and baby brother. Thirty years later, Joanna is a successful doctor with a baby of her own when the madman is released from prison. Regina Chase is Joanna's precocious sixteen-year-old mother's assistant; Neil Hunter, Joanna's husband, is an entrepreneur with big troubles. <br/><br/>Police detective Louise Monroe, recently married herself, is attempting to protect a woman and her children from an abusi</span>
  <span id="freeText14400351877946674320" style="display:none">Joanna Mason, a six-year-old girl, was the only person to escape when a madman killed her mother, sister and baby brother. Thirty years later, Joanna is a successful doctor with a baby of her own when the madman is released from prison. Regina Chase is Joanna's precocious sixteen-year-old mother's assistant; Neil Hunter, Joanna's husband, is an entrepreneur with big troubles. <br /><br />Police detective Louise Monroe, recently married herself, is attempting to protect a woman and her children from an abusive husband and is also participating in the investigation into a suspicious fire at one of Neil Hunter's properties. Ex-cop and P.I. Jackson Brodie who has always been enamored of Louise, has family difficulties of his own.<br /><br />All of their lives intersect over a four-day period containing a number of near-cataclysmic events. Atkinson weaves the detailed story lines together in a very interesting book which is really more of a character study than it is a crime novel. All of these characters are interesting and their stories combine in a great climax. This is a very good read, but one should not be expecting to find here a very traditional crime novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14400351877946674320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText695226375388613720" style="display:none">Oh this was so good! Great characters, great story, great writing. In this book Kate Atkinson pulls together all the different threads of her story so well. It follows four different characters to start and you’re not sure how they will all intersect. Jackson is his usual put upon self, I’m not sure why he works as a central character but he does. The other main characters, Louise and the other police around her (particularly Marcus) and her new husband is one thread. Then we have Dr Hunter who has a tragedy in her childhood. And lastly Reggie Chase, a clever 16yo orphan, my favourite in this book. A lot of the subject matter is nasty crime, accidents and misfortunes for the various people in it but it’s a satisfying, enjoyable read! </span>

<div id="review_38793450" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38793450" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38793450?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/323906-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38793450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5907567266911414700">Kate Atkinson was, for me, a slowly acquired taste. I'd read 'Case Histories' and 'One Good Turn' and, while I found much to admire in each book, I ended up keeping my distance, put off by the violent quirkiness of her plots and characters. In fact, I remember so little about her first book, the 1995 Whitbread Book of the Year,'Behind the Scenes at the Museum,' that I must have dropped it after the first few pages.<br/>'When Will There Be Good News', her most recent book, made me a fan. There's plent</span>
  <span id="freeText5907567266911414700" style="display:none">Kate Atkinson was, for me, a slowly acquired taste. I'd read 'Case Histories' and 'One Good Turn' and, while I found much to admire in each book, I ended up keeping my distance, put off by the violent quirkiness of her plots and characters. In fact, I remember so little about her first book, the 1995 Whitbread Book of the Year,'Behind the Scenes at the Museum,' that I must have dropped it after the first few pages.<br />'When Will There Be Good News', her most recent book, made me a fan. There's plenty that's quirky and violent here, of course, but there are characters I grew very fond of and whose fates really mattered to me. Reggie Chase, 16 year old mother's helper and bright, funny, conscientious school leaver, is one such character, and her employer, generous and accomplished Dr. Joanna Hunter, survivor of an unspeakably sad childhood, is another. Add Jackson Brodie, ex-policeman, permanently hapless hero of Atkinson's earlier novels and Louise Monroe, Deputy Chief Inspector, Brodie's foil and perennial crush, and, bingo, you've got redemption and balance for all that bloodshed and depravity. <br />I'm now such an admirer of Atkinson that I'm going back to read/reread her first novel and I'm going to order her 'Human Croquet,' too. Converts are the staunchest believers.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="5907567266911414700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11134158813568834830">The first few Atkinson books I read I was kind of "meh" about. I didn't really love them, but I liked her writing enough to keep trying. Then she published the first two Jackson Brodie books and I enjoyed them enormously. And then, although I kept adding all her new books to my TBR list, somehow none of them ever made it to the top. Don't be like me. Put Atkinson at the top of your list. [I've got A God in Ruins standing by as soon as I finish this other book, and the others are at the top of th</span>
  <span id="freeText11134158813568834830" style="display:none">The first few Atkinson books I read I was kind of "meh" about. I didn't really love them, but I liked her writing enough to keep trying. Then she published the first two Jackson Brodie books and I enjoyed them enormously. And then, although I kept adding all her new books to my TBR list, somehow none of them ever made it to the top. Don't be like me. Put Atkinson at the top of your list. [I've got A God in Ruins standing by as soon as I finish this other book, and the others are at the top of the queue]. The Brodie books in particular hit that sweet spot of examining the after effects of a crime like Barbara Vine, or Laura Lippman, while also being a compelling read, an entertaining mystery, and a Literary Novel.<br /><br />Good stuff.<br /><br />Library copy</span>

<div id="review_34834944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34834944" />
    <a title="LJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/250195-lj"><img alt="LJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436467895p2/250195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34834944?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LJ" href="/user/show/250195-lj">LJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385608015" href="/book/show/3749300-when-will-there-be-good-news">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=contemporary_post_1945">contemporary_post_1945</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=female_author">female_author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34834944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11346799985475955153">WHEN WILL THERE BE GOOD NEWS? (Pol Proc-Jackson Brodie-England-Cont) – Ex<br/>Atkinson, Kate – 3rd in Jackson Brodie series<br/>Doubleday, 2008, UK Hardcover – ISBN: 9780385608015<br/><br/>First Sentence: The heat rising up from the tarmac seemed to get trapped between the thick hedges that towered above their heads like battlements.<br/><br/>Dr. Joanna Hunter (nee’ Mason) is the only survivor of an attack that killed her mother, sister and brother. Now, thirty years later, the man responsible has been released from prison. </span>
  <span id="freeText11346799985475955153" style="display:none">WHEN WILL THERE BE GOOD NEWS? (Pol Proc-Jackson Brodie-England-Cont) – Ex<br />Atkinson, Kate – 3rd in Jackson Brodie series<br />Doubleday, 2008, UK Hardcover – ISBN: 9780385608015<br /><br />First Sentence: The heat rising up from the tarmac seemed to get trapped between the thick hedges that towered above their heads like battlements.<br /><br />Dr. Joanna Hunter (nee’ Mason) is the only survivor of an attack that killed her mother, sister and brother. Now, thirty years later, the man responsible has been released from prison. Ex-detective Jackson Brodie, the one to find young Joanna after the attack, is traveling by train when it derails. Sixteen-year-old Reggie, although she looks to be only 12 but has an old soul, is a mother’s help for Joanna’s baby, Gabriel, and is being tutored by Ms. MacDonald in exchange for errands. Ms. MacDonald’s property backs onto a railway line. The lives of these four people intersect in a completely unexpected manner.<br /><br />What an unusual and wonderful book! The plot is not always easy to follow, nor is it always easy to keep the characters straight, but it has some of the best dialogue I’ve ever read and philosophical insights that made me pause. It had a captivating beginning where I was drawn into the sights, smells and sounds only to be followed by the terror and regret of the scene. <br /><br />The main characters were wonderful and fully-developed through the course of the story. Reggie—“…Reggie’s life was like the Ilian plain, littered with the dead.”--, in particular, is an absolute marvel and I really thought of this as her story to the point where I didn’t want it to end and I do want to know what happens to her in the future. She became just that real. <br /><br />The author provides an excellent sense of place, but it is absolutely the characters that drive this story. There are a lot of coincidences—“A coincidence is just an explanation waiting to happen.”—but they play into the story and life is full of coincidences. <br /><br />This book is not for everyone; some might find the style confusing or slow. On one hand, I would not want to be a character in this story as there are more dead people surrounding the characters than I believe I’ve ever read. On the other there were times I laughed out loud, mainly due to the author’s wonderful dialogue. It’s of the level where you want to read it aloud to others. I do wish I had learned Latin, but the internet is very useful. <br /><br />I’ve not read the previous two books in this series and felt no lack of them for knowing the characters or plot in this book, but I certainly do want to go back and read them for the pure joy of indulging in Ms. Atkinson’s writing. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11346799985475955153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
